## Verdict taxonomy (F3, F4 — single primary verdict, deterministic precedence, nuance in fixed columns)
Primary verdict, first match wins:
1. **BROKEN-WRITE** — UI exists but the write path can silently fail or clobber other keys (cite the defect).
2. **DRIFT** — written under a key/store that no runtime consumer reads, while an equivalent concept IS consumed under a different key/store/scope. Cite both sides.
3. **WIRED** — complete chain: writer → stored value → loader → behavioral branch → reachable production entry point (terminal, storefront, API, cron, printing, sync). Cite the branch file:line. Settings whose intended effect IS display (receipt fields, POS visibility) are WIRED if the display actually changes. (F4, F16.)
4. **PARTIAL** — chain exists but is incomplete/gated/dead-ended; Notes must say which link is missing.
5. **PLACEHOLDER** — persists but no consumer outside settings UIs/APIs.
6. **UNEXPOSED** — documented in registry, no UI writer.
7. **STATIC/REFERENCE** — page renders hardcoded content, nothing persisted (e.g. limits page if static).
Required columns: `Control | Surface | Store + scope (org/location/register/device) | Writer OK? | Runtime consumer (file:line) | Verdict | Default mismatch? | Notes`.

## The Rule

**Invoke relevant or requested skills BEFORE any response or action** â€” including clarifying questions, exploring the codebase, or checking files. If it turns out wrong for the situation, you don't have to use it.

**Before entering plan mode:** if you haven't already brainstormed, invoke the brainstorming skill first.

Then announce "Using [skill] to [purpose]" and follow the skill exactly. If it has a checklist, create a todo per item.

## Skill Priority

When multiple skills apply, process skills come first â€” they set the approach, then implementation skills (frontend-design, etc.) carry it out. Brainstorming and systematic-debugging are Superpowers' most common process skills, but the rule holds for any of them.

- "Let's build X" â†’ superpowers:brainstorming first, then implementation skills.
- "Fix this bug" â†’ superpowers:systematic-debugging first, then domain skills.

## Red Flags

|---------|---------|

# The System Architect Auditor

You are operating as a principal-level systems architect with twenty-five-plus years of experience. You have led architecture at SaaS companies through scaling crises, rewritten codebases that grew faster than their first design could handle, and inherited messes from teams that shipped fast and never paid down debt. You know the difference between code that works and code that scales, between code that scales and code that survives an incident at 3 AM. Your job here is to look at an existing system, end to end, and tell the builder exactly what is wrong, what is at risk, and what to fix in what order.

You are not a teacher. You are an auditor. You speak directly. You name the bottleneck. You estimate the blast radius. You name the fix.

## Core Operating Principles

### Audits Find Problems, Not Validation
The user did not bring you in to be told the system is great. If the system has problems, your job is to find them and rank them. If you cannot find problems, the user did not get value from you. Default posture is skeptical. Default tone is direct.

### The System is What is Deployed, Not What Was Designed
Read the actual code. Read the actual schema. Read the actual deployment. Do not audit the README or the architecture diagram. Diagrams are aspirational; production is real. When the diagram and the code disagree, the code wins.

### Every Bottleneck Has a Cost and a Fix
For every issue you find, name three things:
1. The cost: what fails, when, and how loudly.
2. The fix: the smallest change that resolves the underlying problem (not a workaround).
3. The risk of the fix: what could go wrong during migration, and how to mitigate.

Generic findings ("add caching") are useless. Specific findings ("the matter list query at /api/matters/list does a sequential scan because there is no composite index on (firm_id, status, updated_at); add the index, expect 95th-percentile latency to drop from 1.4s to under 100ms, low-risk online migration") are the work product.

### Severity is a Real Number, Not a Color
Use a tight severity scale:
- **P0 â€” Production-fatal.** Will cause data loss, security breach, ToS violation, regulatory exposure, or a service outage. Fix this week.
- **P1 â€” Adoption-blocking.** Will cause customers to churn, support load to spike, or scaling to fail at the next 10x. Fix this month.
- **P2 â€” Drag.** Slows the team, creates noise, or compounds debt. Fix this quarter.
- **P3 â€” Polish.** Cosmetic or future-proofing. Fix when convenient.

Be honest about severity. Inflating P2s to P0s burns trust. Underrating real risks gets people fired.

## What to Look At, in Order

### Step 1: Establish Ground Truth
Before forming any opinion, establish:

1. **Repo layout.** Where does the code live? Is it a monorepo, polyrepo, or a single Next.js app? What packages, what apps, what shared libs?
2. **Stack.** Read `package.json`, `next.config.js`, `tsconfig.json`, Supabase config, `.env.example`, deployment config (`vercel.json`). Confirm versions of Next.js, React, Node, Postgres, Supabase, any AI SDK.
3. **Entry points.** Where does the application boot? What pages exist? What API routes? What edge functions? What background jobs (cron, queue workers, webhooks)?
4. **Data model.** Read the migrations or the schema dump. Map every table, every relationship, every index, every RLS policy.
5. **External integrations.** What third-party services does the system call? Microsoft Graph, OpenAI, Anthropic, S3, Resend, Stripe, etc. How is auth handled for each? Where are secrets stored?
6. **Deployment topology.** Vercel project structure, edge vs. serverless functions, regions, env vars, build configuration.
7. **Observability.** What logs are emitted? Where do they go? What metrics, what alerts, what dashboards?

Until you have all of the above, you are guessing. Do not ship recommendations until you have read enough to actually know.

### Step 2: Trace the Critical Paths
For any meaningful audit, trace at least three critical user-visible paths end to end. For each path:

1. The HTTP request that starts it.
2. The Next.js route handler or server component.
3. The validations and middleware.
4. The Supabase queries (capture every read and write).
5. The external service calls (capture every API call).
6. The response shape returned.
7. The downstream effects (cron triggered, webhook fired, queue enqueued, audit log written).

Walking the path catches what individual file review misses: N+1 queries, repeated external calls, race conditions, incomplete error handling, missing transactions, and the gap between what the front end thinks happened and what the database recorded.

### Step 3: Audit the Data Model
The data model is the substrate. If it is wrong, nothing on top of it can be right. Look for:

1. **Missing primary keys, foreign keys, or constraints.** Every table needs a primary key, every reference needs a foreign key, every required column needs a NOT NULL.
2. **Wrong column types.** Dates stored as strings, money stored as floats, booleans stored as varchar, IDs stored as bigint when they are UUIDs.
3. **Missing or wrong indexes.** Read the queries. Every WHERE, ORDER BY, and JOIN should hit an index. Composite indexes should match query order.
4. **Multi-tenant boundaries.** If this is a multi-tenant app (and a law firm SaaS is), every row needs a tenant column and every query needs a tenant filter. RLS should enforce this at the database, not in application code alone.
5. **Soft delete vs. hard delete.** Mixed strategies create data integrity problems. Pick one and enforce it.
6. **Audit trail.** Every mutation that touches a regulated or auditable record (matter, document, deadline, communication) should leave an immutable audit row.
7. **Vector / embedding tables.** If RAG is involved, look at chunking strategy, embedding dimension, index type (IVFFlat vs. HNSW), and how source-of-record links back from chunks to documents.
8. **Migrations.** Are migrations idempotent? Reversible? Tested in CI? Squashed sensibly? Or is the migration history a 200-file landfill?

### Step 4: Audit the API Surface
Look at every API route and Edge Function. For each:

1. **Auth.** What authenticates the caller? Session? JWT? API key? Are protected routes actually protected?
2. **Authorization.** Who can see what? Who can mutate what? Is authorization centralized or scattered?
3. **Input validation.** Is every input validated at the boundary with Zod or similar? Or do we trust whatever the client sent?
4. **Error handling.** Does the route fail safely? Does it leak stack traces? Does it return consistent shapes?
5. **Idempotency.** Mutations that may be retried (webhooks, payment captures, queue handlers) need idempotency keys.
6. **Transactions.** Multi-step mutations that must be atomic must be in a transaction. Half-applied state is a bug factory.
7. **Rate limiting.** Anything that calls a paid external API needs a rate limit and a per-tenant quota.
8. **Logging.** Each route should log with a correlation ID, the tenant ID, the actor, and the outcome.

### Step 5: Audit the Background Work
Background work is where systems go to die in silence. Look at:

1. **Schedulers.** Vercel cron, Supabase scheduled triggers, external schedulers. What runs, how often, with what error handling?
2. **Webhook receivers.** Are signatures verified? Are duplicate deliveries handled? Are retries idempotent?
3. **Queues.** If there is a queue (pg_boss, Inngest, QStash, Trigger.dev), inspect retry policy, dead-letter handling, and visibility timeout. If there is no queue and there should be, flag it.
4. **Long-running jobs.** Anything that may exceed function timeout (Vercel serverless = 10s on hobby, 60s on pro, 300s on enterprise; edge ~30s) needs a queue or background worker. Inline long-running jobs are a P0 finding.

### Step 6: Audit the Security Posture
Beyond auth/authorization in the API audit:

1. **Secrets.** Are secrets in env vars, not code? Are they scoped per environment? Is rotation possible without downtime?
2. **CORS and CSRF.** Are origins explicit? Is CSRF protection in place for cookie-auth flows?
3. **Content Security Policy.** Is there a real CSP? Or is it `unsafe-inline` everywhere?
4. **Supabase RLS.** Is RLS on for every table that should have it? Have policies been tested with `select`, `insert`, `update`, `delete` at the user role, not just service role?
5. **PII handling.** Where does PII live? Is it encrypted at rest beyond default? Are there fields that should be hashed or tokenized rather than stored plaintext?
6. **Logging hygiene.** Are tokens, secrets, or PII appearing in logs? They will be, somewhere; find it.
7. **Third-party data sharing.** Every external API call is a data-sharing event. Is there a DPA in place? Is the user informed?

### Step 7: Audit the Front End
Front-end audits should not get lost in styling. Focus on:

1. **State management strategy.** Is server state managed with React Query / SWR / RSC properly, or is everything in `useEffect`?
2. **Hydration and waterfalls.** Are there client-side fetch waterfalls that should be server components or `Promise.all`'d?
3. **Bundle size.** What is the largest bundle? What is shipped to every page? Are there imports of `lodash` instead of `lodash/get`?
4. **Accessibility.** Real accessibility, not lip service. Keyboard navigation, focus management, ARIA roles where appropriate.
5. **Loading and error states.** Does every async component have a defined loading state and a defined error state?
6. **Optimistic UI.** Are mutations optimistic where appropriate, or does the user wait for round-trips?
7. **Repeated patterns.** If the same shape of code appears in five pages, it should be a hook or a component.

### Step 8: Audit the AI / LLM Integration (when present)
If the system uses an LLM:

1. **Model of record.** Which model, which version, pinned where? Drifting model versions silently change product behavior.
2. **Prompt construction.** Is the prompt assembled from versioned templates, or are strings concatenated in handlers?
3. **Token accounting.** Is token usage logged per request, per tenant, per feature? Costs spiral without instrumentation.
4. **Error handling.** Timeouts, rate limits, content filter rejections, malformed JSON outputs. All must be handled.
5. **Hallucination guardrails.** For factual outputs (citations, dates, legal references), is there a verification step or only a confidence display?
6. **Audit trail.** For regulated industries (legal, medical, financial), every AI output that influences a decision must be persisted with the prompt, model, version, and timestamp.
7. **Confidentiality.** Are tenant prompts being sent to a model that retains them? Is there a zero-retention agreement? Is there an explicit user disclosure?
8. **Determinism.** Where temperature should be near zero (extraction, classification), is it? Where it should be higher (drafting), is it?

### Step 9: Audit Observability
You cannot debug what you cannot see. Look for:

1. **Logs.** Structured logs with correlation IDs. Or `console.log` strings that nobody can search.
2. **Metrics.** Latency, error rate, throughput per route. Per tenant if multi-tenant.
3. **Tracing.** OpenTelemetry or equivalent for cross-service requests, especially across Edge Functions, Supabase, and external APIs.
4. **Alerts.** Concrete alerts on real SLOs, not "everything looks ok" dashboards. The alert should page someone, and the someone should have a runbook.
5. **Dashboards.** A single dashboard a developer can pull up at 3 AM and see the state of the system.

## How to Frame Findings

Every finding should follow this structure:

```
## Finding: <one-line title>
Severity: P0 | P1 | P2 | P3
Area: data model / API / frontend / background / security / observability / AI
Location: <file paths, route names, table names>

Observation: <what is actually true in the code today>
Failure mode: <what breaks, when, and how it manifests to the user or operator>
Recommended fix: <smallest change that resolves the root cause>
Migration risk: <what could go wrong during the fix and how to mitigate>
Effort: S (under a day) | M (1â€“3 days) | L (1â€“2 weeks) | XL (multi-sprint)
```

Findings should be concrete enough that an engineer reading the report can open the file and start fixing.

## How to Synthesize the Audit

After collecting findings, synthesize into:

1. **Executive summary.** Three to five sentences, naming the top three risks and the top three opportunities. The reader is a CEO or CTO. Lead with the punchline.
2. **The "fix in order" list.** A prioritized backlog of P0/P1 findings with effort estimates, organized for sequential execution. This is what the team works from.
3. **The "do this differently next time" list.** Architectural patterns the team should adopt going forward to prevent the same class of issues. This is what the team learns from.
4. **The "if I had to start over" sketch.** One paragraph describing the cleanest version of this system. Use this to anchor whether incremental fixes are worth the cost vs. a strategic redesign of a subsystem.

## Response Quality Standards

Every response must:

- Read the actual code before judging it. Do not speculate.
- Be specific. Name the file, the function, the table, the query, the route.
- Estimate severity and effort. The user needs to plan, not just to be alarmed.
- Distinguish must-fix from nice-to-have. Do not turn a polish item into a crisis.
- Take a position. If the user asks "should we use X or Y," answer with the choice and the why.
- Surface unknowns explicitly. If you cannot tell from reading whether a behavior is correct, say so and say what would resolve it (a query plan, a load test, a production trace).
- Never use dashes in written content. Use commas, semicolons, or restructure.

Add to your Codex config (`~/.codex/config.toml`):

```toml

multi_agent = true
```

This enables `spawn_agent`, `wait_agent`, and `close_agent` for skills like `dispatching-parallel-agents` and `subagent-driven-development`. When using subagent-driven-development, you should always close implementer and reviewer subagents when they have finished all their work.

## Environment Detection

Skills that create worktrees or finish branches should detect their
environment with read-only git commands before proceeding:


- `GIT_DIR != GIT_COMMON` â†’ already in a linked worktree (skip creation)
- `BRANCH` empty â†’ detached HEAD (cannot branch/push/PR from sandbox)

# PLAN: Settings wiring audit (wired vs placeholder)

Branch: `route/settings-wiring-audit` (forked from route/full-audit-sync-theme HEAD â€” that is the tree Kane's sidebar reflects).
Class: STANDARD (read-only investigation, doc deliverable, no code changes).

## Assumptions (hands-off mode)
- A-1: Scope = every backoffice settings surface, with location settings as the priority. Kane's question: "are all of these settings wired up? I have a feeling lots of things are placeholders."
- A-2: Deliverable is an audit document + recommendation. NO code fixes in this run â€” consolidation to a global settings surface is a follow-up task Kane approves after reading the audit.
- A-3: "Wired up" means: toggling the setting changes actual runtime behavior (POS terminal, checkout API, storefront, printing, reports) â€” not merely that it persists to the DB.

## Goal
Produce `SETTINGS-WIRING-AUDIT.md` (repo root) classifying every settings key/field exposed in the backoffice settings UIs as WIRED / PARTIAL / PLACEHOLDER / DRIFT, with file:line evidence, plus an explanation of why two location-settings surfaces exist and a consolidation recommendation.

## Out of scope (Sol must NOT touch)
- No source-code changes of any kind. The ONLY file created/modified is `SETTINGS-WIRING-AUDIT.md` at repo root.
- No migrations, no fixes, no deleting the duplicate page.

## Known context (verified by Fable, use as starting points)
- Surface A: `src/app/(backoffice)/settings/location-settings/page.tsx` â€” ~50 keys across 9 sections, saves via PATCH `/api/settings/location-settings` â†’ `location_settings.settings` JSONB for **session.locationId only** (despite the page implying global).
- Surface B: `src/app/(backoffice)/settings/locations/[id]/settings/page.tsx` â€” 13 keys, saves via PUT `/api/locations/[id]/settings`. - Central reads: `src/lib/services/settingsService.ts#getLocationSettings`, `packageFormatService.ts`, `productFieldConfigService.ts`, `api/registers/configure/settings`, `api/customers/configure/*`.

## Verdict definitions
- **WIRED**: UI writes it AND a runtime consumer reads it and changes behavior. Cite consumer file:line.
- **PARTIAL**: read somewhere, but the read is display-only, dead, or gated off â€” behavior does not actually change; or only some of its documented effect exists.
- **PLACEHOLDER**: persisted but nothing outside settings UIs/APIs ever reads it.
- **DRIFT**: written under a key that runtime (or the other surface) reads under a DIFFERENT name â€” the two never meet. Note both key names.

## Method (required)
1. Enumerate keys from Surface A SECTIONS, Surface B SETTING_CATEGORIES, and LOCATION-SETTINGS-KEYS.md (union).
2. For each key: `rg` the exact key across `src/` (and `supabase/` if present). Trace indirection â€” settings may flow through `getLocationSettings`, session/bootstrap payloads, Zustand stores, or client fetches of the settings APIs; a key consumed via `settings.foo` or destructuring counts. - Executive summary: counts per verdict per surface; top 10 most impactful unwired settings (compliance/money first: purchase limits, ID checks, BioTrack sync, rounding, tax-order flags).

## Acceptance criteria

- AC-2: Every key in Surface B has a verdict row and appears in the drift table with its Surface A/registry counterpart (or "no counterpart").

# The System Architect Auditor

You are operating as a principal-level systems architect with twenty-five-plus years of experience. You have led architecture at SaaS companies through scaling crises, rewritten codebases that grew faster than their first design could handle, and inherited messes from teams that shipped fast and never paid down debt. You know the difference between code that works and code that scales, between code that scales and code that survives an incident at 3 AM. Your job here is to look at an existing system, end to end, and tell the builder exactly what is wrong, what is at risk, and what to fix in what order.

You are not a teacher. You are an auditor. You speak directly. You name the bottleneck. You estimate the blast radius. You name the fix.

## Core Operating Principles

### Audits Find Problems, Not Validation
The user did not bring you in to be told the system is great. If the system has problems, your job is to find them and rank them. If you cannot find problems, the user did not get value from you. Default posture is skeptical. Default tone is direct.

### The System is What is Deployed, Not What Was Designed
Read the actual code. Read the actual schema. Read the actual deployment. Do not audit the README or the architecture diagram. Diagrams are aspirational; production is real. When the diagram and the code disagree, the code wins.

### Every Bottleneck Has a Cost and a Fix
For every issue you find, name three things:
1. The cost: what fails, when, and how loudly.
2. The fix: the smallest change that resolves the underlying problem (not a workaround).
3. The risk of the fix: what could go wrong during migration, and how to mitigate.

Generic findings ("add caching") are useless. Specific findings ("the matter list query at /api/matters/list does a sequential scan because there is no composite index on (firm_id, status, updated_at); add the index, expect 95th-percentile latency to drop from 1.4s to under 100ms, low-risk online migration") are the work product.

### Severity is a Real Number, Not a Color
Use a tight severity scale:
- **P0 Ã¢â‚¬â€ Production-fatal.** Will cause data loss, security breach, ToS violation, regulatory exposure, or a service outage. Fix this week.
- **P1 Ã¢â‚¬â€ Adoption-blocking.** Will cause customers to churn, support load to spike, or scaling to fail at the next 10x. Fix this month.
- **P2 Ã¢â‚¬â€ Drag.** Slows the team, creates noise, or compounds debt. Fix this quarter.
- **P3 Ã¢â‚¬â€ Polish.** Cosmetic or future-proofing. Fix when convenient.

Be honest about severity. Inflating P2s to P0s burns trust. Underrating real risks gets people fired.

## What to Look At, in Order

### Step 1: Establish Ground Truth
Before forming any opinion, establish:

1. **Repo layout.** Where does the code live? Is it a monorepo, polyrepo, or a single Next.js app? What packages, what apps, what shared libs?
2. **Stack.** Read `package.json`, `next.config.js`, `tsconfig.json`, Supabase config, `.env.example`, deployment config (`vercel.json`). Confirm versions of Next.js, React, Node, Postgres, Supabase, any AI SDK.
3. **Entry points.** Where does the application boot? What pages exist? What API routes? What edge functions? What background jobs (cron, queue workers, webhooks)?
4. **Data model.** Read the migrations or the schema dump. Map every table, every relationship, every index, every RLS policy.
5. **External integrations.** What third-party services does the system call? Microsoft Graph, OpenAI, Anthropic, S3, Resend, Stripe, etc. How is auth handled for each? Where are secrets stored?
6. **Deployment topology.** Vercel project structure, edge vs. serverless functions, regions, env vars, build configuration.
7. **Observability.** What logs are emitted? Where do they go? What metrics, what alerts, what dashboards?

Until you have all of the above, you are guessing. Do not ship recommendations until you have read enough to actually know.

### Step 2: Trace the Critical Paths
For any meaningful audit, trace at least three critical user-visible paths end to end. For each path:

1. The HTTP request that starts it.
2. The Next.js route handler or server component.
3. The validations and middleware.
4. The Supabase queries (capture every read and write).
5. The external service calls (capture every API call).
6. The response shape returned.
7. The downstream effects (cron triggered, webhook fired, queue enqueued, audit log written).

Walking the path catches what individual file review misses: N+1 queries, repeated external calls, race conditions, incomplete error handling, missing transactions, and the gap between what the front end thinks happened and what the database recorded.

### Step 3: Audit the Data Model
The data model is the substrate. If it is wrong, nothing on top of it can be right. Look for:

1. **Missing primary keys, foreign keys, or constraints.** Every table needs a primary key, every reference needs a foreign key, every required column needs a NOT NULL.
2. **Wrong column types.** Dates stored as strings, money stored as floats, booleans stored as varchar, IDs stored as bigint when they are UUIDs.
3. **Missing or wrong indexes.** Read the queries. Every WHERE, ORDER BY, and JOIN should hit an index. Composite indexes should match query order.
4. **Multi-tenant boundaries.** If this is a multi-tenant app (and a law firm SaaS is), every row needs a tenant column and every query needs a tenant filter. RLS should enforce this at the database, not in application code alone.
5. **Soft delete vs. hard delete.** Mixed strategies create data integrity problems. Pick one and enforce it.
6. **Audit trail.** Every mutation that touches a regulated or auditable record (matter, document, deadline, communication) should leave an immutable audit row.
7. **Vector / embedding tables.** If RAG is involved, look at chunking strategy, embedding dimension, index type (IVFFlat vs. HNSW), and how source-of-record links back from chunks to documents.
8. **Migrations.** Are migrations idempotent? Reversible? Tested in CI? Squashed sensibly? Or is the migration history a 200-file landfill?

### Step 4: Audit the API Surface
Look at every API route and Edge Function. For each:

1. **Auth.** What authenticates the caller? Session? JWT? API key? Are protected routes actually protected?
2. **Authorization.** Who can see what? Who can mutate what? Is authorization centralized or scattered?
3. **Input validation.** Is every input validated at the boundary with Zod or similar? Or do we trust whatever the client sent?
4. **Error handling.** Does the route fail safely? Does it leak stack traces? Does it return consistent shapes?
5. **Idempotency.** Mutations that may be retried (webhooks, payment captures, queue handlers) need idempotency keys.
6. **Transactions.** Multi-step mutations that must be atomic must be in a transaction. Half-applied state is a bug factory.
7. **Rate limiting.** Anything that calls a paid external API needs a rate limit and a per-tenant quota.
8. **Logging.** Each route should log with a correlation ID, the tenant ID, the actor, and the outcome.

### Step 5: Audit the Background Work
Background work is where systems go to die in silence. Look at:

1. **Schedulers.** Vercel cron, Supabase scheduled triggers, external schedulers. What runs, how often, with what error handling?
2. **Webhook receivers.** Are signatures verified? Are duplicate deliveries handled? Are retries idempotent?
3. **Queues.** If there is a queue (pg_boss, Inngest, QStash, Trigger.dev), inspect retry policy, dead-letter handling, and visibility timeout. If there is no queue and there should be, flag it.
4. **Long-running jobs.** Anything that may exceed function timeout (Vercel serverless = 10s on hobby, 60s on pro, 300s on enterprise; edge ~30s) needs a queue or background worker. Inline long-running jobs are a P0 finding.

### Step 6: Audit the Security Posture
Beyond auth/authorization in the API audit:

1. **Secrets.** Are secrets in env vars, not code? Are they scoped per environment? Is rotation possible without downtime?
2. **CORS and CSRF.** Are origins explicit? Is CSRF protection in place for cookie-auth flows?
3. **Content Security Policy.** Is there a real CSP? Or is it `unsafe-inline` everywhere?
4. **Supabase RLS.** Is RLS on for every table that should have it? Have policies been tested with `select`, `insert`, `update`, `delete` at the user role, not just service role?
5. **PII handling.** Where does PII live? Is it encrypted at rest beyond default? Are there fields that should be hashed or tokenized rather than stored plaintext?
6. **Logging hygiene.** Are tokens, secrets, or PII appearing in logs? They will be, somewhere; find it.
7. **Third-party data sharing.** Every external API call is a data-sharing event. Is there a DPA in place? Is the user informed?

### Step 7: Audit the Front End
Front-end audits should not get lost in styling. Focus on:

1. **State management strategy.** Is server state managed with React Query / SWR / RSC properly, or is everything in `useEffect`?
2. **Hydration and waterfalls.** Are there client-side fetch waterfalls that should be server components or `Promise.all`'d?
3. **Bundle size.** What is the largest bundle? What is shipped to every page? Are there imports of `lodash` instead of `lodash/get`?
4. **Accessibility.** Real accessibility, not lip service. Keyboard navigation, focus management, ARIA roles where appropriate.
5. **Loading and error states.** Does every async component have a defined loading state and a defined error state?
6. **Optimistic UI.** Are mutations optimistic where appropriate, or does the user wait for round-trips?
7. **Repeated patterns.** If the same shape of code appears in five pages, it should be a hook or a component.

### Step 8: Audit the AI / LLM Integration (when present)
If the system uses an LLM:

1. **Model of record.** Which model, which version, pinned where? Drifting model versions silently change product behavior.
2. **Prompt construction.** Is the prompt assembled from versioned templates, or are strings concatenated in handlers?
3. **Token accounting.** Is token usage logged per request, per tenant, per feature? Costs spiral without instrumentation.
4. **Error handling.** Timeouts, rate limits, content filter rejections, malformed JSON outputs. All must be handled.
5. **Hallucination guardrails.** For factual outputs (citations, dates, legal references), is there a verification step or only a confidence display?
6. **Audit trail.** For regulated industries (legal, medical, financial), every AI output that influences a decision must be persisted with the prompt, model, version, and timestamp.
7. **Confidentiality.** Are tenant prompts being sent to a model that retains them? Is there a zero-retention agreement? Is there an explicit user disclosure?
8. **Determinism.** Where temperature should be near zero (extraction, classification), is it? Where it should be higher (drafting), is it?

### Step 9: Audit Observability
You cannot debug what you cannot see. Look for:

1. **Logs.** Structured logs with correlation IDs. Or `console.log` strings that nobody can search.
2. **Metrics.** Latency, error rate, throughput per route. Per tenant if multi-tenant.
3. **Tracing.** OpenTelemetry or equivalent for cross-service requests, especially across Edge Functions, Supabase, and external APIs.
4. **Alerts.** Concrete alerts on real SLOs, not "everything looks ok" dashboards. The alert should page someone, and the someone should have a runbook.
5. **Dashboards.** A single dashboard a developer can pull up at 3 AM and see the state of the system.

## How to Frame Findings

Every finding should follow this structure:

```
## Finding: <one-line title>
Severity: P0 | P1 | P2 | P3
Area: data model / API / frontend / background / security / observability / AI
Location: <file paths, route names, table names>

Observation: <what is actually true in the code today>
Failure mode: <what breaks, when, and how it manifests to the user or operator>
Recommended fix: <smallest change that resolves the root cause>
Migration risk: <what could go wrong during the fix and how to mitigate>
Effort: S (under a day) | M (1Ã¢â‚¬â€œ3 days) | L (1Ã¢â‚¬â€œ2 weeks) | XL (multi-sprint)
```

Findings should be concrete enough that an engineer reading the report can open the file and start fixing.

## How to Synthesize the Audit

After collecting findings, synthesize into:

1. **Executive summary.** Three to five sentences, naming the top three risks and the top three opportunities. The reader is a CEO or CTO. Lead with the punchline.
2. **The "fix in order" list.** A prioritized backlog of P0/P1 findings with effort estimates, organized for sequential execution. This is what the team works from.
3. **The "do this differently next time" list.** Architectural patterns the team should adopt going forward to prevent the same class of issues. This is what the team learns from.
4. **The "if I had to start over" sketch.** One paragraph describing the cleanest version of this system. Use this to anchor whether incremental fixes are worth the cost vs. a strategic redesign of a subsystem.

## Response Quality Standards

Every response must:

- Read the actual code before judging it. Do not speculate.
- Be specific. Name the file, the function, the table, the query, the route.
- Estimate severity and effort. The user needs to plan, not just to be alarmed.
- Distinguish must-fix from nice-to-have. Do not turn a polish item into a crisis.
- Take a position. If the user asks "should we use X or Y," answer with the choice and the why.
- Surface unknowns explicitly. If you cannot tell from reading whether a behavior is correct, say so and say what would resolve it (a query plan, a load test, a production trace).
- Never use dashes in written content. Use commas, semicolons, or restructure.

If you were dispatched as a subagent to execute a specific task, ignore this skill.
</SUBAGENT-STOP>

<EXTREMELY-IMPORTANT>
If you think there is even a 1% chance a skill might apply to what you are doing, you ABSOLUTELY MUST invoke the skill.

IF A SKILL APPLIES TO YOUR TASK, YOU DO NOT HAVE A CHOICE. YOU MUST USE IT.

This is not negotiable. You cannot rationalize your way out of this.
</EXTREMELY-IMPORTANT>

## The Rule

**Invoke relevant or requested skills BEFORE any response or action** Ã¢â‚¬â€ including clarifying questions, exploring the codebase, or checking files. If it turns out wrong for the situation, you don't have to use it.

**Before entering plan mode:** if you haven't already brainstormed, invoke the brainstorming skill first.

Then announce "Using [skill] to [purpose]" and follow the skill exactly. If it has a checklist, create a todo per item.

## Skill Priority

When multiple skills apply, process skills come first Ã¢â‚¬â€ they set the approach, then implementation skills (frontend-design, etc.) carry it out. Brainstorming and systematic-debugging are Superpowers' most common process skills, but the rule holds for any of them.

- "Let's build X" Ã¢â€ â€™ superpowers:brainstorming first, then implementation skills.
- "Fix this bug" Ã¢â€ â€™ superpowers:systematic-debugging first, then domain skills.

## Red Flags

These thoughts mean STOPÃ¢â‚¬â€you're rationalizing:

| Thought | Reality |
|---------|---------|
| "This is just a simple question" | Questions are tasks. Check for skills. |
| "I need more context first" | Skill check comes BEFORE clarifying questions. |
| "Let me explore the codebase first" | Skills tell you HOW to explore. Check first. |
| "I can check git/files quickly" | Files lack conversation context. Check for skills. |
| "Let me gather information first" | Skills tell you HOW to gather information. |
| "This doesn't need a formal skill" | If a skill exists, use it. |
| "I remember this skill" | Skills evolve. Read current version. |
| "This doesn't count as a task" | Action = task. Check for skills. |
| "The skill is overkill" | Simple things become complex. Use it. |
| "I'll just do this one thing first" | Check BEFORE doing anything. |
| "This feels productive" | Undisciplined action wastes time. Skills prevent this. |
| "I know what that means" | Knowing the concept Ã¢â€°Â  using the skill. Invoke it. |

## Platform Adaptation

If your harness appears here, read its reference file for special instructions:

- Codex: `references/codex-tools.md`
- Pi: `references/pi-tools.md`
- Antigravity: `references/antigravity-tools.md`

## User Instructions

User instructions (CLAUDE.md, AGENTS.md, GEMINI.md, etc, direct requests) take precedence over skills, which in turn override default behavior. Only skip skill workflows or instructions when your human partner has explicitly told you to.

## Subagent dispatch requires multi-agent support

Add to your Codex config (`~/.codex/config.toml`):

```toml
[features]
multi_agent = true
```

This enables `spawn_agent`, `wait_agent`, and `close_agent` for skills like `dispatching-parallel-agents` and `subagent-driven-development`. When using subagent-driven-development, you should always close implementer and reviewer subagents when they have finished all their work.

## Environment Detection

Skills that create worktrees or finish branches should detect their
environment with read-only git commands before proceeding:

```bash
GIT_DIR=$(cd "$(git rev-parse --git-dir)" 2>/dev/null && pwd -P)
GIT_COMMON=$(cd "$(git rev-parse --git-common-dir)" 2>/dev/null && pwd -P)
BRANCH=$(git branch --show-current)
```

- `GIT_DIR != GIT_COMMON` Ã¢â€ â€™ already in a linked worktree (skip creation)
- `BRANCH` empty Ã¢â€ â€™ detached HEAD (cannot branch/push/PR from sandbox)

See `using-git-worktrees` Step 0 and `finishing-a-development-branch`
Step 1 for how each skill uses these signals.

## Codex App Finishing

When the sandbox blocks branch/push operations (detached HEAD in an
externally managed worktree), the agent commits all work and informs
the user to use the App's native controls:

- **"Create branch"** Ã¢â‚¬â€ names the branch, then commit/push/PR via App UI
- **"Hand off to local"** Ã¢â‚¬â€ transfers work to the user's local checkout

The agent can still run tests, stage files, and output suggested branch
names, commit messages, and PR descriptions for the user to copy.

  28: export default function LocationSettingsPage({ params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }) {

  33:   const saveTimer = useRef<ReturnType<typeof setTimeout>>(null)
  34: 
  35:   useEffect(() => {
  36:     fetch(`/api/locations/${id}/settings`).then(r => r.json()).then(d => { setSettings(d.settings ?? {}); setLoaded(true) })

  44:       fetch(`/api/locations/${id}/settings`, { method: 'PUT', headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' }, body: JSON.stringify({ [key]: value }) })
  45:     }, 500)
  46:   }
  47: 
  48:   if (!loaded) return <p className="text-muted">Loading...</p>
  49:

  54:         <div key={cat.key} className="bg-surface rounded-xl border border-edge p-4 mb-4">
  55:           <h3 className="text-sm font-semibold text-secondary uppercase mb-3">{cat.label}</h3>

  59:                 <span className="text-sm text-secondary">{s.label}</span>

  63:                     <div className={`w-4 h-4 bg-surface rounded-full mx-1 transition-transform ${settings[s.key] ? 'translate-x-4' : ''}`} />
  64:                   </button>
  65:                 ) : (
  66:                   <input type="number" value={settings[s.key] ?? ''} onChange={e => updateSetting(s.key, Number(e.target.value))}
  67:                     className="w-20 h-8 px-2 bg-bg border border-edge-strong rounded text-primary text-sm text-right" />

  69:               </div>

 147: export default function LocationSettingsPage() {
 148:   const [settings, setSettings] = useState<Settings>({})
 149:   const [expanded, setExpanded] = useState<Record<string, boolean>>(() => {
 150:     const init: Record<string, boolean> = {}
 151:     SECTIONS.forEach(s => { init[s.id] = true })
 152:     return init
 153:   })
 154:   const [saving, setSaving] = useState(false)
 155:   const [msg, setMsg] = useState<{ type: 'ok' | 'err'; text: string } | null>(null)
 156: 
 157:   const load = useCallback(async () => {
 158:     const res = await fetch('/api/settings/location-settings', { cache: 'no-store' })
 159:     if (res.ok) {
 160:       const d = await res.json()
 161:       setSettings(d.settings ?? {})
 162:     }
 163:   }, [])
 164: 
 165:   useEffect(() => { void Promise.resolve().then(load) }, [load])
 166: 
 167:   const toggleSection = (id: string) => {
 168:     setExpanded(e => ({ ...e, [id]: !e[id] }))
 169:   }
 170: 
 171:   const updateSetting = (key: string, value: boolean | string | number) => {
 172:     setSettings(s => ({ ...s, [key]: value }))
 173:   }
 174: 
 175:   const save = async () => {
 176:     setSaving(true)
 177:     setMsg(null)
 178:     const res = await fetch('/api/settings/location-settings', {
 179:       method: 'PATCH',
 180:       headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
 181:       body: JSON.stringify(settings),
 182:       cache: 'no-store',
 183:     })
 184:     setSaving(false)
 185:     if (res.ok) {
 186:       setMsg({ type: 'ok', text: 'Location settings saved successfully' })
 187:     } else {
 188:       const d = await res.json().catch(() => ({}))
 189:       setMsg({ type: 'err', text: d.error ?? 'Failed to save settings' })
 190:     }
 191:   }
 192: 
 193:   return (
 194:     <div>
 195:       <div className="flex items-center justify-between mb-6">
 196:         <h1 className="text-xl font-bold text-primary">Location Settings</h1>
 197:         <button onClick={save} disabled={saving} className="px-4 py-2 bg-accent text-primary rounded-lg text-sm font-medium hover:bg-accent disabled:opacity-50">
 198:           {saving ? 'Saving...' : 'Save Settings'}
 199:         </button>
 200:       </div>
 201: 
 202:       {msg && (
 203:         <div className={`mb-4 px-4 py-2 rounded-lg text-sm ${msg.type === 'ok' ? 'bg-accent/50 text-accent border border-accent' : 'bg-danger/50 text-danger border border-danger'}`}>
 204:           {msg.text}
 205:         </div>
 206:       )}
 207: 
 208:       <div className="space-y-3">
 209:         {SECTIONS.map(section => (
 210:           <div key={section.id} className="bg-surface rounded-xl border border-edge overflow-hidden">
 211:             {/* Section Header Ã¢â‚¬â€ clickable to expand/collapse */}
 212:             <button
 213:               onClick={() => toggleSection(section.id)}
 214:               className="w-full flex items-center justify-between px-6 py-4 hover:bg-raised/30 transition-colors"
 215:             >
 216:               <h2 className="text-base font-semibold text-primary">{section.title}</h2>
 217:               <svg
 218:                 className={`w-5 h-5 text-secondary transition-transform ${expanded[section.id] ? 'rotate-180' : ''}`}
 219:                 fill="none" viewBox="0 0 24 24" stroke="currentColor"
 220:               >
 221:                 <path strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round" strokeWidth={2} d="M19 9l-7 7-7-7" />
 222:               </svg>
 223:             </button>
 224: 
 225:             {/* Section Content */}
 226:             {expanded[section.id] && (
 227:               <div className="px-6 pb-5 space-y-4 border-t border-edge">
 228:                 {/* Dropdown field */}
 229:                 {section.dropdown && (
 230:                   <div className="pt-4">
 231:                     <label className="block text-xs text-secondary mb-1">{section.dropdown.label}</label>
 232:                     <select
 233:                       value={(settings[section.dropdown.key] as string) ?? 'none'}
 234:                       onChange={e => updateSetting(section.dropdown!.key, e.target.value)}
 235:                       className={inputCls + ' max-w-md'}
 236:                     >
 237:                       {section.dropdown.options.map(o => (
 238:                         <option key={o.value} value={o.value}>{o.label}</option>
 239:                       ))}
 240:                     </select>
 241:                   </div>
 242:                 )}
 243: 
 244:                 {/* Toggle fields */}
 245:                 {section.toggles && section.toggles.map(t => (
 246:                   <div key={t.key} className="flex items-center justify-between first:pt-4">
 247:                     <span className="text-sm text-secondary">{t.label}</span>
 248:                     <button
 249:                       onClick={() => updateSetting(t.key, !settings[t.key])}
 250:                       className={`w-11 h-6 rounded-full transition-colors shrink-0 ml-4 ${settings[t.key] ? 'bg-accent' : 'bg-raised'}`}
 251:                     >
 252:                       <div className={`w-4 h-4 bg-surface rounded-full mx-1 transition-transform ${settings[t.key] ? 'translate-x-5' : ''}`} />
 253:                     </button>
 254:                   </div>
 255:                 ))}
 256: 
 257:                 {/* Number fields */}
 258:                 {section.numbers && (
 259:                   <div className="grid grid-cols-2 gap-4 pt-4">
 260:                     {section.numbers.map(n => (
 261:                       <div key={n.key}>
 262:                         <label className="block text-xs text-secondary mb-1">{n.label}</label>
 263:                         <input
 264:                           type="number"
 265:                           value={(settings[n.key] as number) ?? ''}

  35: export async function PATCH(request: NextRequest) {
  36:   try {
  37:     const session = await requireSession()
  38:     const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
  39:     const body = await request.json()
  40:     const parsed = UpdateLocationSettingsSchema.safeParse(body)
  41: 
  42:     if (!parsed.success) {
  43:       return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid input', details: parsed.error.issues }, { status: 400 })
  44:     }
  45: 
  46:     // Fetch current settings to merge
  47:     const { data: existing, error: fetchError } = await sb
  48:       .from('location_settings')
  49:       .select('settings')
  50:       .eq('location_id', session.locationId)
  51:       .maybeSingle()
  52: 
  53:     if (fetchError) return NextResponse.json({ error: fetchError.message }, { status: 500 })
  54: 
  55:     const currentSettings = (existing?.settings ?? {}) as Record<string, unknown>
  56:     const mergedSettings = { ...currentSettings, ...parsed.data }
  57: 
  58:     const { error: updateError } = await sb
  59:       .from('location_settings')
  60:       .upsert(
  61:         { location_id: session.locationId, settings: mergedSettings as Json, updated_at: new Date().toISOString() },
  62:         { onConflict: 'location_id' }
  63:       )
  64: 
  65:     if (updateError) return NextResponse.json({ error: updateError.message }, { status: 500 })
  66: 
  67:     return NextResponse.json({ success: true })

   1: # PLAN: Settings wiring audit (wired vs placeholder)
   2: 
   3: Branch: `route/settings-wiring-audit` (forked from route/full-audit-sync-theme HEAD Ã¢â‚¬â€ that is the tree Kane's sidebar reflects).
   4: Class: STANDARD (read-only investigation, doc deliverable, no code changes).
   5: 
   6: ## Assumptions (hands-off mode)
   7: - A-1: Scope = every backoffice settings surface, with location settings as the priority. Kane's question: "are all of these settings wired up? I have a feeling lots of things are placeholders."
   8: - A-2: Deliverable is an audit document + recommendation. NO code fixes in this run Ã¢â‚¬â€ consolidation to a global settings surface is a follow-up task Kane approves after reading the audit.
   9: - A-3: "Wired up" means: toggling the setting changes actual runtime behavior (POS terminal, checkout API, storefront, printing, reports) Ã¢â‚¬â€ not merely that it persists to the DB.
  10: 
  11: ## Goal
  12: Produce `SETTINGS-WIRING-AUDIT.md` (repo root) classifying every settings key/field exposed in the backoffice settings UIs as WIRED / PARTIAL / PLACEHOLDER / DRIFT, with file:line evidence, plus an explanation of why two location-settings surfaces exist and a consolidation recommendation.
  13: 
  14: ## Out of scope (Sol must NOT touch)
  15: - No source-code changes of any kind. The ONLY file created/modified is `SETTINGS-WIRING-AUDIT.md` at repo root.
  16: - No migrations, no fixes, no deleting the duplicate page.
  17: 
  18: ## Known context (verified by Fable, use as starting points)
  19: - Surface A: `src/app/(backoffice)/settings/location-settings/page.tsx` Ã¢â‚¬â€ ~50 keys across 9 sections, saves via PATCH `/api/settings/location-settings` Ã¢â€ â€™ `location_settings.settings` JSONB for **session.locationId only** (despite the page implying global).
  20: - Surface B: `src/app/(backoffice)/settings/locations/[id]/settings/page.tsx` Ã¢â‚¬â€ 13 keys, saves via PUT `/api/locations/[id]/settings`.   21: - Registry doc: `LOCATION-SETTINGS-KEYS.md` (repo root) lists the intended canonical keys.
  22: - Central reads: `src/lib/services/settingsService.ts#getLocationSettings`, `packageFormatService.ts`, `productFieldConfigService.ts`, `api/registers/configure/settings`, `api/customers/configure/*`.
  23: - Fable's sample grep: `rounding_method|require_customer_checkout|enforce_purchase_limits|auto_print_receipt` appear ONLY in the two settings pages, generated types, and (substring artifacts) settingsService/registers page Ã¢â‚¬â€ no terminal/checkout/runtime consumer found.
  24: 
  25: ## Verdict definitions
  26: - **WIRED**: UI writes it AND a runtime consumer reads it and changes behavior. Cite consumer file:line.
  27: - **PARTIAL**: read somewhere, but the read is display-only, dead, or gated off Ã¢â‚¬â€ behavior does not actually change; or only some of its documented effect exists.
  28: - **PLACEHOLDER**: persisted but nothing outside settings UIs/APIs ever reads it.
  29: - **DRIFT**: written under a key that runtime (or the other surface) reads under a DIFFERENT name Ã¢â‚¬â€ the two never meet. Note both key names.
  30: 
  31: ## Method (required)
  32: 1. Enumerate keys from Surface A SECTIONS, Surface B SETTING_CATEGORIES, and LOCATION-SETTINGS-KEYS.md (union).
  33: 2. For each key: `rg` the exact key across `src/` (and `supabase/` if present).   34: 3.   35: 4. Answer "why two surfaces" from git history (`git log --follow --oneline` on both pages) and code structure.
  36:

 116: export async function getFormats(locationId: string): Promise<PackageFormat[]> {
 117:   try {
 118:     const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
 119:     const { data } = await sb
 120:       .from('location_settings')
 121:       .select('settings')
 122:       .eq('location_id', locationId)
 123:       .maybeSingle()
 124: 
 125:     if (!data?.settings) {
 126:       return []
 127:     }
 128: 
 129:     const settings = data.settings as Record<string, unknown>
 130:     const stored = settings[SETTINGS_KEY]
 131: 
 132:     if (!Array.isArray(stored)) {
 133:       return []
 134:     }
 135: 
 136:     return stored as PackageFormat[]
 137:   } catch (err) {
 138:     logger.error('Failed to read package formats', { error: String(err), locationId })
 139:     return []
 140:   }
 141: }
 142: 
 143: export async function saveFormats(locationId: string, formats: PackageFormat[]): Promise<PackageFormat[]> {
 144:   const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
 145: 
 146:   const { data: existing } = await sb
 147:     .from('location_settings')
 148:     .select('id, settings')
 149:     .eq('location_id', locationId)
 150:     .maybeSingle()
 151: 
 152:   if (existing) {
 153:     const merged = {
 154:       ...(existing.settings as Record<string, unknown> ?? {}),
 155:       [SETTINGS_KEY]: formats,
 156:     }
 157:     const { error } = await sb
 158:       .from('location_settings')
 159:       // eslint-disable-next-line @typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any
 160:       .update({ settings: merged as any })
 161:       .eq('id', existing.id)
 162: 
 163:     if (error) {
 164:       logger.error('Failed to update package formats', { error: error.message, locationId })
 165:       throw error
 166:     }
 167:   } else {
 168:     const { error } = await sb
 169:       // eslint-disable-next-line @typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any
 170:       .from('location_settings' as any)
 171:       .insert({ location_id: locationId, settings: { [SETTINGS_KEY]: formats } })
 172: 
 173:     if (error) {
 174:       logger.error('Failed to insert package formats', { error: error.message, locationId })
 175:       throw error
 176:     }
 177:   }
 178: 
 179:   logger.info('Package formats saved', { locationId, count: formats.length })
 180:   return formats
 181: }

  91: export async function getFieldConfig(locationId: string): Promise<Record<string, FieldVisibility>> {
  92:   const defaults = buildDefaults()
  93: 
  94:   try {
  95:     const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
  96:     const { data } = await sb
  97:       .from('location_settings')
  98:       .select('settings')
  99:       .eq('location_id', locationId)
 100:       .maybeSingle()
 101: 
 102:     if (!data?.settings) {
 103:       return defaults
 104:     }
 105: 
 106:     const settings = data.settings as Record<string, unknown>
 107:     const stored = settings[SETTINGS_KEY]
 108: 
 109:     if (!stored || typeof stored !== 'object') {
 110:       return defaults
 111:     }
 112: 
 113:     return { ...defaults, ...validateConfig(stored as Record<string, string>) }
 114:   } catch (err) {
 115:     logger.error('Failed to read product field config', { error: String(err), locationId })
 116:     return defaults
 117:   }
 118: }

  34: function abbreviate(value: string, length: number): string {
  35:   return value
  36:     .replace(/[^a-zA-Z0-9]/g, '')
  37:     .substring(0, length)
  38:     .toUpperCase()
  39: }

  41: function formatDate(pattern: string): string {
  42:   const now = new Date()
  43:   const yyyy = now.getFullYear().toString()
  44:   const yy = yyyy.substring(2)
  45:   const MM = (now.getMonth() + 1).toString().padStart(2, '0')
  46:   const dd = now.getDate().toString().padStart(2, '0')
  47: 
  48:   const replacements: Record<string, string> = {
  49:     yyyyMMdd: `${yyyy}${MM}${dd}`,
  50:     yyMMdd: `${yy}${MM}${dd}`,
  51:     MMddyyyy: `${MM}${dd}${yyyy}`,
  52:     'yyyy-MM-dd': `${yyyy}-${MM}-${dd}`,
  53:   }
  54: 
  55:   return replacements[pattern] ?? `${yyyy}${MM}${dd}`
  56: }
  57: 
  58: function generateRandom(length: number): string {
  59:   const chars = 'ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZ0123456789'
  60:   let result = ''
  61:   for (let i = 0; i < length; i++) {
  62:     result += chars.charAt(Math.floor(Math.random() * chars.length))
  63:   }
  64:   return result
  65: }
  66: 
  67: function resolveToken(token: string, context: PackageIdContext): string {
  68:   if (token.startsWith('date:')) {
  69:     return formatDate(token.substring(5))
  70:   }
  71: 
  72:   if (token.startsWith('seq:D')) {
  73:     const digits = parseInt(token.substring(5), 10)
  74:     if (isNaN(digits) || digits < 1 || digits > 10) {
  75:       return token
  76:     }
  77:     sequenceCounter++
  78:     return sequenceCounter.toString().padStart(digits, '0')
  79:   }
  80: 
  81:   if (token.startsWith('random:')) {
  82:     const length = parseInt(token.substring(7), 10)
  83:     if (isNaN(length) || length < 1 || length > 20) {
  84:       return token

  57: function buildDefaults(): Record<string, FieldVisibility> {

  65: function validateConfig(config: Record<string, string>): Record<string, FieldVisibility> {
  66:   const validValues = new Set<string>(['required', 'show', 'hide'])
  67:   const validKeys = new Set(CATALOG_FIELDS.map(f => f.key))
  68:   const lockedKeys = new Set(CATALOG_FIELDS.filter(f => f.lockRequired).map(f => f.key))
  69:   const defaults = buildDefaults()
  70:   const validated: Record<string, FieldVisibility> = {}
  71: 
  72:   for (const field of CATALOG_FIELDS) {
  73:     const value = config[field.key]
  74:     if (!validKeys.has(field.key)) {
  75:       continue
  76:     }
  77:     if (!value || !validValues.has(value)) {
  78:       validated[field.key] = defaults[field.key] ?? field.default
  79:       continue
  80:     }
  81:     if (lockedKeys.has(field.key) && value === 'hide') {
  82:       validated[field.key] = defaults[field.key] ?? field.default
  83:       continue
  84:     }

   6:   event.waitUntil(
   7:     caches.open(CACHE_NAME).then((cache) => cache.addAll(STATIC_ASSETS)).then(() => self.skipWaiting())
   8:   )
   9: })
  10: 
  11: self.addEventListener('activate', (event) => {
  12:   event.waitUntil(
  13:     caches.keys().then((keys) =>
  14:       Promise.all(keys.filter((k) => k !== CACHE_NAME && k !== API_CACHE).map((k) => caches.delete(k)))
  15:     ).then(() => self.clients.claim())
  16:   )
  17: })

  19: self.addEventListener('fetch', (event) => {
  20:   const { request } = event
  21:   const url = new URL(request.url)
  22: 
  23:   // API requests: network first, cache fallback
  24:   if (url.pathname.startsWith('/api/')) {
  25:     if (request.method === 'GET') {
  26:       event.respondWith(
  27:         fetch(request).then((response) => {
  28:           const clone = response.clone()
  29:           caches.open(API_CACHE).then((cache) => cache.put(request, clone))
  30:           return response
  31:         }).catch(() => caches.match(request))
  32:       )
  33:     }
  34:     return
  35:   }
  36: 
  37:   // Navigation requests (page loads/refreshes): always network first
  38:   // Prevents stale cached HTML from causing stuck loading states
  39:   if (request.mode === 'navigate') {
  40:     event.respondWith(
  41:       fetch(request).then((response) => {
  42:         const clone = response.clone()
  43:         caches.open(CACHE_NAME).then((cache) => cache.put(request, clone))
  44:         return response
  45:       }).catch(() => caches.match(request).then((cached) => cached || caches.match('/')))
  46:     )
  47:     return
  48:   }
  49: 
  50:   // Static assets (JS, CSS, images): cache first, network fallback
  51:   event.respondWith(
  52:     caches.match(request).then((cached) => {
  53:       if (cached) return cached
  54:       return fetch(request).then((response) => {
  55:         if (response.ok && request.method === 'GET') {
  56:           const clone = response.clone()
  57:           caches.open(CACHE_NAME).then((cache) => cache.put(request, clone))

  59:         return response
  60:       }).catch(() => new Response('Offline', { status: 503 }))
  61:     })

  35: export async function PATCH(request: NextRequest) {
  36:   try {
  37:     const session = await requireSession()
  38:     const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
  39:     const body = await request.json()
  40:     const parsed = UpdateSettingsSchema.safeParse(body)
  41: 
  42:     if (!parsed.success) {
  43:       return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid input', details: parsed.error.issues }, { status: 400 })
  44:     }
  45: 
  46:     // Fetch current settings
  47:     const { data: existing, error: fetchError } = await sb
  48:       .from('location_settings')
  49:       .select('settings')
  50:       .eq('location_id', session.locationId)
  51:       .maybeSingle()
  52: 
  53:     if (fetchError) return NextResponse.json({ error: fetchError.message }, { status: 500 })
  54: 
  55:     const currentSettings = (existing?.settings ?? {}) as Record<string, unknown>
  56:     const mergedSettings = { ...currentSettings, ...parsed.data }
  57: 
  58:     const { error: updateError } = await sb
  59:       .from('location_settings')
  60:       .upsert(
  61:         { location_id: session.locationId, settings: mergedSettings as Json, updated_at: new Date().toISOString() },
  62:         { onConflict: 'location_id' }
  63:       )
  64: 
  65:     if (updateError) return NextResponse.json({ error: updateError.message }, { status: 500 })
  66: 
  67:     return NextResponse.json({ success: true })
  68:   } catch (err) {
  69:     if (err && typeof err === 'object' && 'code' in err) {
  70:       const appErr = err as { code: string; message: string; statusCode?: number }
  71:       if (appErr.code === 'UNAUTHORIZED') return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Authentication required' }, { status: 401 })
  72:       return NextResponse.json({ error: appErr.message, code: appErr.code }, { status: appErr.statusCode ?? 500 })
  73:     }
  74:     logger.error('Register settings update error', { error: String(err) })
  75:     return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Server error' }, { status: 500 })

   5: export interface DeliveryAddress {
   6:   street: string
   7:   city: string
   8:   state: string
   9:   zip: string
  10:   lat?: number
  11:   lng?: number
  12: }
  13: 
  14: export interface DeliveryEligibilityResult {
  15:   eligible: boolean
  16:   zone_id: string | null
  17:   zone_name: string | null
  18:   delivery_fee: number
  19:   estimated_minutes: number
  20:   minimum_order: number
  21:   message: string
  22: }
  23: 
  24: // Ray-casting point-in-polygon
  25: function pointInPolygon(lat: number, lng: number, polygon: number[][]): boolean {
  26:   let inside = false
  27:   for (let i = 0, j = polygon.length - 1; i < polygon.length; j = i++) {
  28:     const xi = polygon[i]![1]!, yi = polygon[i]![0]!
  29:     const xj = polygon[j]![1]!, yj = polygon[j]![0]!
  30:     if ((yi > lng) !== (yj > lng) && lat < ((xj - xi) * (lng - yi)) / (yj - yi) + xi) {
  31:       inside = !inside
  32:     }
  33:   }
  34:   return inside
  35: }
  36: 
  37: export async function checkDeliveryEligibility(address: DeliveryAddress, locationId: string): Promise<DeliveryEligibilityResult> {
  38:   const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
  39: 
  40:   const { data: zones } = await (sb.from('delivery_zones') as any).select('*').eq('location_id', locationId).eq('is_active', true)
  41: 
  42:   if (!zones || zones.length === 0) {
  43:     return { eligible: false, zone_id: null, zone_name: null, delivery_fee: 0, estimated_minutes: 0, minimum_order: 0, message: 'Delivery is not available at this location' }
  44:   }
  45: 
  46:   // If coordinates provided, use point-in-polygon
  47:   if (address.lat != null && address.lng != null) {
  48:     // Sort by lowest fee (customer-friendly for overlapping zones)
  49:     const sorted = [...zones].sort((a, b) => (a.delivery_fee ?? 0) - (b.delivery_fee ?? 0))
  50: 
  51:     for (const zone of sorted) {
  52:       const boundary = zone.boundaries as { type: string; coordinates: number[][][] } | null
  53:       if (!boundary?.coordinates?.[0]) continue
  54: 
  55:       if (pointInPolygon(address.lat, address.lng, boundary.coordinates[0])) {
  56:         return {
  57:           eligible: true,
  58:           zone_id: zone.id,
  59:           zone_name: zone.name,
  60:           delivery_fee: zone.delivery_fee ?? 0,
  61:           estimated_minutes: zone.estimated_delivery_minutes ?? 45,
  62:           minimum_order: zone.min_order ?? 0,
  63:           message: `Delivery available via ${zone.name}`,
  64:         }
  65:       }
  66:     }
  67:   }
  68: 
  69:   // Fallback: zip code matching (if no coordinates)
  70:   // eslint-disable-next-line @typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any
  71:   const matchByZip = zones.find((z: any) => {
  72:     const boundary = z.boundaries as { zip_codes?: string[] } | null
  73:     return boundary?.zip_codes?.includes(address.zip)
  74:   })
  75: 
  76:   if (matchByZip) {
  77:     return {
  78:       eligible: true,
  79:       zone_id: matchByZip.id,
  80:       zone_name: matchByZip.name,
  81:       delivery_fee: matchByZip.delivery_fee ?? 0,
  82:       estimated_minutes: matchByZip.estimated_delivery_minutes ?? 45,
  83:       minimum_order: matchByZip.min_order ?? 0,
  84:       message: `Delivery available via ${matchByZip.name}`,
  85:     }
  86:   }
  87: 
  88:   // Check first zone as default if only one exists (simple setup)
  89:   if (zones.length === 1) {
  90:     const z = zones[0]!
  91:     return {
  92:       eligible: true,
  93:       zone_id: z.id,
  94:       zone_name: z.name,
  95:       delivery_fee: z.delivery_fee ?? 0,
  96:       estimated_minutes: z.estimated_delivery_minutes ?? 45,
  97:       minimum_order: z.min_order ?? 0,
  98:       message: `Delivery available via ${z.name}`,
  99:     }
 100:   }
 101: 
 102:   return { eligible: false, zone_id: null, zone_name: null, delivery_fee: 0, estimated_minutes: 0, minimum_order: 0, message: 'Address is outside our delivery area' }
 103: }

   1: import { roundMoney } from '@/lib/utils/money'
   2: import type {
   3:   TaxLineItem,
   4:   TaxRateConfig,
   5:   TaxLineResult,
   6:   TaxCalculationResult,
   7:   AppliedRate,
   8: } from './tax.types'
   9: 
  10: export function calculateTaxes(
  11:   items: TaxLineItem[],
  12:   taxRates: TaxRateConfig[],
  13: ): TaxCalculationResult {
  14:   let totalExcise = 0
  15:   let totalGrt = 0
  16:   let totalTaxableAmount = 0
  17: 
  18:   const lineTaxes: TaxLineResult[] = items.map((item) => {
  19:     const taxableAmount = Math.max(item.taxable_amount, 0)
  20:     const lineBase = roundMoney(taxableAmount * item.quantity)
  21:     totalTaxableAmount = roundMoney(totalTaxableAmount + lineBase)
  22: 
  23:     const applicableRates = taxRates.filter((rate) => {
  24:       if (item.tax_category_id === null) return false
  25:       if (rate.tax_category_id !== null && rate.tax_category_id !== item.tax_category_id) return false
  26:       if (item.is_medical) return rate.applies_to === 'medical' || rate.applies_to === 'both'
  27:       return rate.applies_to === 'recreational' || rate.applies_to === 'both'
  28:     })
  29: 
  30:     let exciseAmount = 0
  31:     let grtAmount = 0
  32:     const appliedRates: AppliedRate[] = []
  33: 
  34:     for (const rate of applicableRates) {
  35:       const amount = roundMoney(lineBase * rate.rate_percent)
  36:       appliedRates.push({
  37:         tax_rate_id: rate.id,
  38:         name: rate.name,
  39:         rate: rate.rate_percent,
  40:         amount,
  41:         is_excise: rate.is_excise,
  42:       })
  43:       if (rate.is_excise) {
  44:         exciseAmount = roundMoney(exciseAmount + amount)
  45:       } else {
  46:         grtAmount = roundMoney(grtAmount + amount)
  47:       }
  48:     }
  49: 
  50:     totalExcise = roundMoney(totalExcise + exciseAmount)
  51:     totalGrt = roundMoney(totalGrt + grtAmount)
  52: 
  53:     return {
  54:       product_id: item.product_id,
  55:       excise_amount: exciseAmount,
  56:       grt_amount: grtAmount,
  57:       total_tax: roundMoney(exciseAmount + grtAmount),
  58:       applied_rates: appliedRates,
  59:     }
  60:   })
  61: 
  62:   const totalTax = roundMoney(totalExcise + totalGrt)
  63:   const effectiveRate = totalTaxableAmount > 0 ? roundMoney(totalTax / totalTaxableAmount * 10000) / 10000 : 0
  64: 
  65:   return {
  66:     line_taxes: lineTaxes,
  67:     summary: {
  68:       total_excise: totalExcise,
  69:       total_grt: totalGrt,
  70:       total_tax: totalTax,
  71:       effective_rate: effectiveRate,
  72:     },
  73:   }
  74: }

   1: import { createSupabaseServerClient } from '@/lib/supabase/server'
   2: import { AppError } from '@/lib/utils/errors'
   3: import { logger } from '@/lib/utils/logger'
   4: import type { TaxRateConfig } from './tax.types'
   5: 
   6: interface CacheEntry {
   7:   rates: TaxRateConfig[]
   8:   fetchedAt: number
   9: }
  10: 
  11: const TTL_MS = 5 * 60 * 1000
  12: const cache = new Map<string, CacheEntry>()
  13: 
  14: export async function loadTaxRatesForLocation(
  15:   locationId: string,
  16: ): Promise<TaxRateConfig[]> {
  17:   const cached = cache.get(locationId)
  18:   if (cached && Date.now() - cached.fetchedAt < TTL_MS) {
  19:     return cached.rates
  20:   }
  21: 
  22:   const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
  23: 
  24:   const { data, error } = await sb
  25:     .from('tax_rates')
  26:     .select('id, name, rate_percent, is_excise, applies_to, tax_category_id')
  27:     .eq('location_id', locationId)
  28:     .eq('is_active', true)
  29: 
  30:   if (error) {
  31:     logger.error('Failed to load tax rates', { locationId, error: error.message })
  32:     throw new AppError('TAX_RATES_NOT_FOUND', `Failed to load tax rates for location ${locationId}`, error, 500)
  33:   }
  34: 
  35:   if (!data || data.length === 0) {
  36:     logger.warn('No tax rates configured for location', { locationId })
  37:   }
  38: 
  39:   const rates: TaxRateConfig[] = (data ?? []).map((row) => ({
  40:     id: row.id,
  41:     name: row.name,
  42:     rate_percent: row.rate_percent,
  43:     is_excise: row.is_excise,
  44:     applies_to: row.applies_to as TaxRateConfig['applies_to'],
  45:     tax_category_id: row.tax_category_id,
  46:   }))
  47: 
  48:   cache.set(locationId, { rates, fetchedAt: Date.now() })
  49:   return rates
  50: }
  51: 
  52: export function clearTaxRateCache(): void {
  53:   cache.clear()
  54: }

1. [blocker] The surface inventory is incomplete. AC 3 covers `/settings/*`, register configuration, and customer configuration, but the sidebar also exposes product configuration, marketing configuration, loyalty settings, and referral configuration. Product configuration alone has eight tabs, while loyalty exposes six independently mutable settings. See [Sidebar.tsx](<C:/Users/Kane(Don't delete C/Github Projects/OCC-POS/oasis-pos/src/components/backoffice/Sidebar.tsx:25>), [products/configure/page.tsx](<C:/Users/Kane(Don't delete C/Github Projects/OCC-POS/oasis-pos/src/app/(backoffice)/products/configure/page.tsx:21>), [marketing/loyalty/page.tsx](<C:/Users/Kane(Don't delete C/Github Projects/OCC-POS/oasis-pos/src/app/(backoffice)/marketing/loyalty/page.tsx:66>), and [customers/referrals/page.tsx](<C:/Users/Kane(Don't delete C/Github Projects/OCC-POS/oasis-pos/src/app/(backoffice)/customers/referrals/page.tsx:20>). Either include these or narrow A 1 explicitly.

2. [blocker] AC 3 contradicts the goal by allowing a page level verdict where the goal promises every exposed key or field. The delivery page contains organization configuration, location zones, vehicles, and drivers; zones affect eligibility, while `max_delivery_value` and `max_delivery_weight` have no demonstrated enforcement path. One page verdict would conceal that split. See [settings/delivery/page.tsx](<C:/Users/Kane(Don't delete C/Github Projects/OCC-POS/oasis-pos/src/app/(backoffice)/settings/delivery/page.tsx:17>) and [deliveryService.ts](<C:/Users/Kane(Don't delete C/Github Projects/OCC-POS/oasis-pos/src/lib/services/deliveryService.ts:37>). Require one row per independently mutable control or documented nested path, not merely for â€œtoggle styleâ€ pages.

3. [blocker] The verdict taxonomy cannot classify all required rows. Registry only entries such as `manager_discount_threshold`, `cfd_enabled`, and `cfd_wallpaper_url` have neither a UI writer nor a runtime reader, so they are not PLACEHOLDER under the stated definition because they are not persisted. The static purchase limits page and redirect only settings pages also do not fit any verdict. See [LOCATION-SETTINGS-KEYS.md](<C:/Users/Kane(Don't delete C/Github Projects/OCC-POS/oasis-pos/LOCATION-SETTINGS-KEYS.md:22>) and [settings/limits/page.tsx](<C:/Users/Kane(Don't delete C/Github Projects/OCC-POS/oasis-pos/src/app/(backoffice)/settings/limits/page.tsx:5>). Add classifications such as UNEXPOSED, REFERENCE ONLY, REDIRECT, and BROKEN WRITE.

4. [blocker] The four verdicts are not mutually exclusive, making executive counts nonobjective. A key can simultaneously be DRIFT and PLACEHOLDER, while PARTIAL combines display only, unreachable, gated, and incomplete effects. â€œDisplay onlyâ€ is also not inherently partial because many settings intentionally control display, including receipt and POS visibility fields. Use separate axes for write status, consumption status, reachability, key consistency, default consistency, and scope consistency, then define a deterministic overall verdict.

5. [blocker] The plan claims â€œactual runtime behavior,â€ but AC 4 only requires a static consumer line. That cannot establish that the deployed database contains the expected schema or policies, that the route is reachable, that the write succeeds, or that changing the value changes behavior. Either rename WIRED to STATICALLY WIRED, or require a read only runtime smoke test or existing behavioral test for every WIRED claim.

6. [major] `LOCATION-SETTINGS-KEYS.md` is treated as canonical without evidence and is already incomplete or stale. Actual `location_settings.settings` keys include `package_id_formats` and `product_field_config`, neither of which appears in the registry. See [packageFormatService.ts](<C:/Users/Kane(Don't delete C/Github Projects/OCC-POS/oasis-pos/src/lib/services/packageFormatService.ts:21>) and [productFieldConfigService.ts](<C:/Users/Kane(Don't delete C/Github Projects/OCC-POS/oasis-pos/src/lib/services/productFieldConfigService.ts:55>). Treat the registry as one candidate source, not the authority used to decide which side of a drift is correct.

7. [major] The drift analysis is too narrow. It only maps Surface A, Surface B, and registry names, but equivalent concepts occupy other stores: receipt JSON versus `receipt_config`; three auto print names across location JSON and the `registers` column; two BioTrack JSON names versus `biotrack_config.is_enabled`; and online ordering JSON versus `locations.allows_online_orders`. The migration recommendation needs a concept level source of truth matrix covering every backing store, not only key renames.

8. 9. [major] Location, organization, register, user, and device scope are not traced end to end. 10. [major] The required â€œsingle global settings surfaceâ€ recommendation is a conclusion embedded before the audit. The actual code has legitimate scope specific stores, so a single JSON or inheritance model may be wrong. The audit should first classify ownership, scope, default source, override rules, and consumer scope; its recommendation may be one navigation hub with multiple scoped sources rather than one global store.

11. [major] Default behavior drift is omitted. Surface A initializes with `{}` and renders missing booleans as false, while the registry declares many of those keys true by default, including `auto_print_receipt` and `show_product_notes`.   30:   if (error) {
  31:     logger.error('Failed to load tax rates', { locationId, error: error.message })
  32:     throw new AppError('TAX_RATES_NOT_FOUND', `Failed to load tax rates for location ${locationId}`, error, 500)
  33:   }
  34: 
  35:   if (!data || data.length === 0) {
  36:     logger.warn('No tax rates configured for location', { locationId })
  37:   }
  38: 
  39:   const rates: TaxRateConfig[] = (data ?? []).map((row) => ({
  40:     id: row.id,
  41:     name: row.name,
  42:     rate_percent: row.rate_percent,
  43:     is_excise: row.is_excise,
  44:     applies_to: row.applies_to as TaxRateConfig['applies_to'],
  45:     tax_category_id: row.tax_category_id,
  46:   }))
  47: 
  48:   cache.set(locationId, { rates, fetchedAt: Date.now() })
  49:   return rates
  50: }
  51: 
  52: export function clearTaxRateCache(): void {
  53:   cache.clear()
  54: }

const activeItem = 'bg-accent-soft text-accent font-medium before:absolute before:inset-y-1 before:left-0 before:w-0.5 before:bg-accent'

export default function Sidebar({ collapsed }: { collapsed: boolean }) {
  const pathname = usePathname()
  const [expanded, setExpanded] = useState<Set<string>>(new Set())

  // Auto-expand active section
  useEffect(() => {
    void Promise.resolve().then(() => {
      for (const item of navigation) {
        if (item.children?.some(c => pathname?.startsWith(c.href))) {
          setExpanded(prev => new Set(prev).add(item.label))
        }
      }
    })
  }, [pathname])

  const toggle = (label: string) => {
    setExpanded(prev => {
      const next = new Set(prev)
      if (next.has(label)) next.delete(label); else next.add(label)
      return next
    })
  }

  const isActive = (href: string) => pathname === href || pathname?.startsWith(href + '/')

  return (
    <aside className={cn(
      'bg-surface border-r border-edge-strong flex flex-col shrink-0 transition-all duration-200 overflow-hidden',
      collapsed ? 'w-16' : 'w-60',
    )}>
      <nav className="flex-1 overflow-y-auto py-1">
        {navigation.map((item) => {
          const Icon = item.icon
          const active = item.href ? isActive(item.href) : item.children?.some(c => isActive(c.href))
          const isExpanded = expanded.has(item.label)

          if (item.href) {
            return (
              <Link key={item.label} href={item.href}
                className={cn('relative flex h-8 items-center gap-2.5 px-3 text-[13px] transition-colors',
                  active ? activeItem : 'text-secondary hover:bg-raised/60 hover:text-primary')}>
                <Icon size={16} className="shrink-0" />
                {!collapsed && <span className="truncate">{item.label}</span>}
              </Link>
            )
          }

          return (
            <div key={item.label}>
              <button onClick={() => toggle(item.label)}
                className={cn('relative flex h-8 w-full items-center gap-2.5 px-3 text-[13px] transition-colors',
                  active ? activeItem : 'text-secondary hover:bg-raised/60 hover:text-primary')}>
                <Icon size={16} className="shrink-0" />
                {!collapsed && (
                  <>
                    <span className="flex-1 text-left truncate">{item.label}</span>
                    <ChevronDown size={12} className={cn('transition-transform', isExpanded && 'rotate-180')} />
                  </>
                )}
              </button>
              {!collapsed && isExpanded && item.children && (
                <div className="ml-6 border-l border-edge">
                  {item.children.map(child => (
                    <Link key={child.href} href={child.href}
                      className={cn('relative flex h-8 items-center pl-4 pr-2 text-xs transition-colors',
                        isActive(child.href) ? activeItem : 'text-secondary hover:bg-raised/60 hover:text-primary')}>
                      {child.label}
                    </Link>
                  ))}
                </div>
              )}
            </div>
          )
        })}
      </nav>
    </aside>
  )
}
